Unknown<===>"     CHAPTER VI.
Unknown<===>I am Inducted into the Cave, and Enlist.
Unknown<===>"Here's the cave," said Jim, at the door of his office, next morning.
Unknown<===>"As prospective joint-proprietor and co-malefactor, I bid you welcome.
Unknown<===>"  The smiles with which the employees resumed their work indicated that the extraordinary character of this welcome was not lost upon them.
Unknown<===>The office was on the ground-floor of one of the more pretentious buildings of Lattimore's main street.
Unknown<===>The post-office was on one side of it, and the First National Bank on the other.
Unknown<===>Over it were the offices of lawyers and physicians.
Unknown<===>It was quite expensively fitted up; and the plate-glass front glittered with gold-and-black sign-lettering.
Unknown<===>The chairs and sofas were upholstered in black leather.
Unknown<===>On the walls hung several decorative advertisements of fire-insurance companies, and maps of the town, county, and state.
Unknown<===>Rolls of tracing-paper and blueprints lay on the flat-topped tables, reminding one of the office of an architect or civil engineer.
Unknown<===>A thin young man worked at books, standing at a high desk; and a plump young woman busily clicked off typewritten matter with an up-to-date machine.
Unknown<===>"You'll find some books and papers on the table in the next room," said Jim, as I finished my first look about.
Unknown<===>"I'll ask you to amuse yourself with 'em for a little while, until I can dispose of my morning's mail; after which we'll resume our hunt for resources.
Unknown<===>We haven't any morning paper yet, and the evening _Herald_ is shipped in by freight and edited with a saw.
Unknown<===>But it's the best we've got--yet.
Unknown<===>"  He read his letters, ran his eyes over his newspapers and a magazine or two, and dictated some correspondence, interrupted occasionally by callers, some of whom he brought into the room where I was whiling away the time, examining maps, and looking over out-of-date copies of the local papers.
Unknown<===>One of these callers was Mr.
Unknown<===>Hinckley, the cashier of the bank, who came to see about some insurance matters.
Unknown<===>He was spare, aquiline, and white-mustached; and very courteously wished Lattimore the good fortune of securing so valuable an acquisition as ourselves.
Unknown<===>It would place Lattimore under additional obligations to Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins, who was proving himself such an effective worker in all public matters.
Unknown<===>"Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins," said he, "has to a wonderful degree identified himself with the material progress of the city.
Unknown<===>He is constantly bringing here enterprising and energetic business men; and we could better afford to lose many an older citizen.
Unknown<===>"  I asked Mr.
Unknown<===>Hinckley as to the length of his own residence in Lattimore.
Unknown<===>"I helped to plat the town, sir," said he.
Unknown<===>"I carried the chain when these streets were surveyed,--a boy just out of Bowdoin College.
Unknown<===>That was in '55.
Unknown<===>I staged it for four hundred miles to get here.
Unknown<===>Aleck Macdonald and I came together, and we've both staid from that day.
Unknown<===>The Indians were camped at the mouth of Brushy Creek; and except for old Pierre Lacroix, a squaw-man, we were for a month the only white men in these parts.
Unknown<===>Then General Lattimore came with a party of surveyors, and by the fall there was quite a village here.
Unknown<===>"  Jim came in with another gentleman, whom he introduced as Captain Tolliver.
Unknown<===>The Captain shook my hand with profuse politeness.
Unknown<===>"I am delighted to see you, suh," said he.
Unknown<===>"Any friend of Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins I shall be proud to know.
Unknown<===>I heah that Mrs.
Unknown<===>Barslow is with you.
Unknown<===>I trust, suh, that she is well.
Unknown<===>"  I informed him that my wife was in excellent health, being completely recovered from the fatigue of her journey.
Unknown<===>"Ah.
Unknown<===>this aiah, this aiah, Mr.
Unknown<===>Barslow.
Unknown<===>It is like wine in its invigorating qualities, like wine, suh.
Unknown<===>Look at Mr.
Unknown<===>Hinckley, hyah, doing the work of two men fo' a lifetime; and younge' now than any of us.
Unknown<===>Come, suh, and make yo' home with us.
Unknown<===>You nevah can regret it.
Unknown<===>Delighted to have you call at my office, suh.
Unknown<===>I am proud to have met you, and hope to become better acquainted with you.
Unknown<===>I hope Mrs.
Unknown<===>Tulliver and Mrs.
Unknown<===>Barslow may soon meet.
Unknown<===>Good-morning, gentlemen.
Unknown<===>" And he hurried out, only to reappear as soon as Mr.
Unknown<===>Hinckley was gone.
Unknown<===>"By the way, Mr.
Unknown<===>Barslow," he whispered, "should you come to Lattimore, as I have no doubt you will, I have some of the choicest residence property in the city, which I shall be mo' than glad to show you.
Unknown<===>Title perfect, no commissions to pay, city water, gas, and electric light in prospect.
Unknown<===>Cain't yo' come and look it ovah now, suh.
Unknown<===>"  "Who is this Captain Tolliver, Jim," I asked as we went out of the office together, "and what is he.
Unknown<===>"  "In other words, 'Who and what art thou, execrable shape.
Unknown<===>' Well, now, don't ask me.
Unknown<===>I've known him for years; in fact, he suggested to me the possibilities of this burg.
Unknown<===>In a way, the city is indebted to him for my presence here.
Unknown<===>But don't ask me about him--study him.
Unknown<===>And don't buy lots from him.
Unknown<===>The Captain has his failings, but he has also his strong points and his uses; and I'll be mistaken if he isn't cast for a fairly prominent part in the drama we're about to put on here.
Unknown<===>But don't spoil your enjoyment by having him described to you.
Unknown<===>Let him dawn on you by degrees.
Unknown<===>"  That day I met most of the prominent men of the town.
Unknown<===>Jim took me into the banks, the shops, and the offices of the leading professional gentlemen.
Unknown<===>He informed them that I was considering the matter of coming to live among them; and I found them very friendly, and much interested in our proposed change of residence.
Unknown<===>They all treated Jim with respect, and his manner toward them had a dignity which I had not looked for.
Unknown<===>Evidently he was making himself felt in the community.
Unknown<===>When we returned to the Centropolis at noon, we found Mrs.
Unknown<===>Trescott and her daughter chatting with my wife.
Unknown<===>The elder woman was ill-groomed, as are all women of her class in comparison with their town sisters, and angular.
Unknown<===>I knew the type so well that I could read the traces of farm cares in her face and form.
Unknown<===>The serving of gangs of harvesters and threshers, the ever-recurring problems of butter, eggs, and berries, the unflagging fight, without much domestic help, for neatness and order about the house, had impressed their stamp upon Mrs.
Unknown<===>Trescott.
Unknown<===>But she was chatting vivaciously, and assuring Mrs.
Unknown<===>Barslow that such a thing as staying longer in town that morning was impossible.
Unknown<===>"I can feel in my bones," said she, "that there's something wrong at the farm.
Unknown<===>"  "You always have that feeling," said her daughter, "as soon as you pass outside the gate.
Unknown<===>"  "And I'm usually right about it," said Mrs.
Unknown<===>Trescott.
Unknown<===>"It isn't any use.
Unknown<===>My system has got into that condition in which I'm in misery if I'm off that farm.
Unknown<===>Josie drags me away from it sometimes; and I do enjoy meeting people.
Unknown<===>But I like to meet 'em out there the best; and I want to urge you to come often, Mrs.
Unknown<===>Barslow, while you're here.
Unknown<===>And in case you move here, I hope you'll like us and the farm well enough so that we'll see a good deal of you.
Unknown<===>"  I was presented to Mrs.
Unknown<===>Trescott, and reintroduced to the young lady, with whom Alice seemed already on friendly terms.
Unknown<===>I was surprised at this, for she was not prone to sudden friendships.
Unknown<===>There was something so attractive in the girl, however, that it went far to explain the phenomenon.
Unknown<===>For one thing, there was in her manner that same steadiness and calm which I had noticed in her voice in the dusk last night.
Unknown<===>It gave one the impression that she could not be surprised or startled, that she had seen or thought out all possible combinations of events, and knew of their sequences, or adjusted herself to things by some all-embracing rule, by which she attained that repose of hers.
Unknown<===>The surprising thing about it, to my mind, was to find this exterior in Bill Trescott's daughter.
Unknown<===>I had seen the same thing once or twice in people to whom I thought it had come as the fruit of wide experience in the world.
Unknown<===>While Miss Trescott was slim, and rather below the medium in height, she was not at all thin; and had the great mass of ruddy dark hair and fine brown eyes which I remembered so well, and a face which would have been pale had it not been for the tan--the only thing about her which suggested those occupations by which she became her father's "right-hand man.
Unknown<===>" There was intelligence in her face, and a grave smile in her eyes, which rarely extended to her handsome mouth.
Unknown<===>If mature in face, form, and manner, she was young in years--some years younger than Alice.
Unknown<===>I hoped that she might stay to dinner; but she went away with her mother.
Unknown<===>In her absence, I devoted some time to praising her.
Unknown<===>Jim failed to join in my paeans further than to give a general assent; but he grew unaccountably mirthful, as if something good had happened to him of which he had not yet told us.
Unknown<===>"I have invited a few people to my parlors this evening," said he, "and, of course, you will be the guests of honor.
Unknown<===>"  My wife demurred.
Unknown<===>She had nothing to wear, and even if she had, I was without evening dress.
Unknown<===>The thing seemed out of the question.
Unknown<===>"Oh, we can't let that stand in the way," said he.
Unknown<===>"So far as your own toilet is concerned, I have nothing to say except that you are known to be making a hurried visit, and I have an abiding faith, based on your manner of stating your trouble, that it can be remedied.
Unknown<===>I saw your eye take on a far-away look as you planned your costume, even while you were declaring that you couldn't do it.
Unknown<===>Didn't I, now.
Unknown<===>"  "You certainly did not," said Alice; and then I noticed the absorbed look myself.
Unknown<===>"But even if I can manage it, how about Albert.
Unknown<===>"  "I'll tell you about Albert.
Unknown<===>I'll bet two to one there won't be a suit of evening clothes worn.
Unknown<===>The dress suit may come in here with street cars and passenger elevators, but it lacks a good deal of being here yet, except in the most sporadic and infrequent way.
Unknown<===>And this thing is to be so absolutely informal that it would make the natives stare.
Unknown<===>You wouldn't wear it if you had it, Al.
Unknown<===>"  "Who will come.
Unknown<===>" said Mrs.
Unknown<===>Barslow.
Unknown<===>"Oh, a couple of dozen ladies and gentlemen, business men and doctors and lawyers and their women-folks.
Unknown<===>They'll stray in from eight to ten and find something to eat on the sideboard.
Unknown<===>They'll have the happiness of meeting you, and you can see what the people you are thinking of living among and doing business with are like.
Unknown<===>It's a necessary part of your visit; and you can't get out of it now, for I've taken the liberty of making all the arrangements.
Unknown<===>And, as a matter of fact, you don't want to do so, do you, now.
Unknown<===>"  Thus appealed to, Alice consented.
Unknown<===>Nothing was said to me about it, my willingness being presumed.
Unknown<===>The guests that evening were almost exclusively men whom I had met during the day, and members of their families.
Unknown<===>In the absence of any more engaging topic, we discussed Lattimore as our possible future home.
Unknown<===>"I have always felt," said Mr.
Unknown<===>Hinckley, who was one of the guests, "that this is the natural site of a great city.
Unknown<===>These valleys, centering here like the spokes of a wheel, are ready-made railway-routes.
Unknown<===>In the East there is a city of from fifty thousand to three times that, every hundred miles or so.
Unknown<===>Why shouldn't it be so here.
Unknown<===>"  "Suh," said Captain Tolliver, "the thing is inevitable.
Unknown<===>Somewhah in this region will grow up a metropolis.
Unknown<===>Shall it be hyah, o' at Fairchild, o' Angus Falls.
Unknown<===>If the people of Lattimore sit supinely, suh, and let these country villages steal from huh the queenship which God o'dained fo' huh when He placed huh in this commandin' site, then, suh, they ah too base to be wo'thy of the suhvices of gentlemen.
Unknown<===>"  "I've always been taught," said Mrs.
Unknown<===>Trescott, "that the credit of placing her in this site belonged to either Mr.
Unknown<===>Hinckley or General Lattimore.
Unknown<===>"  "Really," said Miss Addison to me, "I don't see how they can laugh at such irreverence.
Unknown<===>"  "I think," said Miss Hinckley in my other ear, "that Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins expressed the whole truth in the matter of the rivalry of these three towns, when he said that when two ride on a horse, one must ride behind.
Unknown<===>Aren't his quotations so--so--illuminating.
Unknown<===>"  I looked about at the company.
Unknown<===>There were Mr.
Unknown<===>Hinckley, Mrs.
Unknown<===>Hinckley, their daughter, whom I recognized as the splendid blonde whose pacers had passed us when we were out driving, Mrs.
Unknown<===>Trescott and her daughter, and Captain and Mrs.
Unknown<===>Tolliver.
Unknown<===>Those present were plainly of several different sets and cliques.
Unknown<===>Mrs.
Unknown<===>Hinckley hoped that my wife would join the Equal Rights Club, and labor for the enfranchisement of women.
Unknown<===>She referred, too, to the eloquence and piety of her pastor, the Presbyterian minister, while Mrs.
Unknown<===>Tolliver quoted Emerson, and invited Alice to join, as soon as we removed, the Monday Club of the Unitarian Church, devoted to the study of his works.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Macdonald, red-whiskered, weather-beaten, and gigantic, fidgeted about the punch-bowl a good deal; and replying to some chance remark made by Alice, ventured the opinion that the grass was gettin' mighty short on the ranges.
Unknown<===>Miss Addison, who came with her cousins the Lattimores, looked with disapproval upon the punch, and disclosed her devotion to the W.
Unknown<===>C.
Unknown<===>T.
Unknown<===>U.
Unknown<===>and the Ladies' Aid Society of the Methodist Church.
Unknown<===>The Lattimores were Will Lattimore and his wife.
Unknown<===>I learned that he was the son of the General, and Jim's lawyer; and that they went rarely into society, being very exclusive.
Unknown<===>This was communicated to me by Mrs.
Unknown<===>Ballard, who brought Miss Ballard with her.
Unknown<===>She asked in tones of the intensest interest if we played whist; while Miss Ballard suggested that about the only way we could find to enjoy ourselves in such a little place would be to identify ourselves with the dancing-party and card-club set.
Unknown<===>I began to suspect that life in Lattimore would not be without its complexities.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Trescott came in for a moment only, for his wife and daughter.
Unknown<===>Miss Trescott was not to be found at first, but was discovered in the bay-window with Jim and Miss Hinckley, looking over some engravings.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins took her down to her carriage, and I thought him a long time gone, for the host.
Unknown<===>As soon as he returned, however, the conversation again turned to the dominant thought of the gathering, municipal expansion.
Unknown<===>And I noted that the points made were Jim's.
Unknown<===>He had already imbued the town with his thoughts, and filled the mouths of its citizens with his arguments.
Unknown<===>After they left, we sat with Jim and talked.
Unknown<===>"Well, how do you like 'em.
Unknown<===>" said he.
Unknown<===>"Why," said Alice, "they're very cordial.
Unknown<===>"  "Heterogeneous, eh.
Unknown<===>" he queried.
Unknown<===>"Yes," said she, "but very cordial.
Unknown<===>I am surprised to feel how little I dislike them.
Unknown<===>"  As for me, I began to look upon Lattimore with more favor.
Unknown<===>I began to catch Jim's enthusiasm and share his confidence.
Unknown<===>As we smoked together in his rooms that evening, he made me the definite proposal that I go into partnership with him.
Unknown<===>We talked about the business, and discussed its possibilities.
Unknown<===>"I don't ask you to believe all my prophecies," said he; "but isn't the situation fairly good, just as it is.
Unknown<===>"  "I think well of it," I answered, "and it's mighty kind of you to ask me to come.
Unknown<===>I'll go as far as to say that if it depends solely on me, we shall come.
Unknown<===>As for these prophecies of yours, I am in candor bound to say that I half believe them.
Unknown<===>"  "Now you _are_ shouting," said he.
Unknown<===>"Never better prophecies anywhere.
Unknown<===>But consider the matter aside from them.
Unknown<===>Then all we clean up in the prophecy department will be velvet, absolute velvet.
Unknown<===>"  "I can add something to the output of the prophecy department," said Alice, when I repeated the phrase; "and that is that there will be some affairs of the heart mingled with the real estate and insurance before long.
Unknown<===>I can see them in embryo now.
Unknown<===>"  "If it's Jim and Miss Trescott you mean, I wish the affair well," said I.
Unknown<===>"I'm quite charmed with her.
Unknown<===>"  "Well," said Alice, "from the standpoint of most men, Miss Hinckley isn't to be left out of the reckoning in such matters.
Unknown<===>What a face and figure she has.
Unknown<===>Miss Addison is too prudish and churchified; but I like Miss Hinckley.
Unknown<===>"  "Yes," said I; "but Miss Trescott seems, somehow, to have been known to one, in some tender and touching relation.
Unknown<===>There's that about her which appeals to one, like some embodiment of the abstract idea of woman.
Unknown<===>That's why one feels as if he had risked his life for her, and protected her, and seen her suffer wrong, and all that--"  "That's only because of that affair you told me of," said my wife.
Unknown<===>"Since I've seen her, I've made up my mind that you misconstrued the matter utterly.
Unknown<===>There was really nothing to it.
Unknown<===>"  In a week I wrote to Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins, accepting his proposal, and promising to close up my affairs, remove to Lattimore, and join with him.
Unknown<===>"I do not feel myself equal to playing the part of either Romulus or Remus in founding your new Rome," I wrote; "but I think as a writer of fire-insurance policies, and keeping the office work up, I may prove myself not entirely a deadhead.
Unknown<===>My wife asks how the breathing-spaces for the populace are coming on.
Unknown<===>"  And the die was cast.
Unknown<===>CHAPTER VII.
Unknown<===>We make our Landing.
Unknown<===>Had I known how cordially our neighbors would greet our return, or how many of them would view our departure with apparently sincere regret, I might have been slower in giving Jim my promise.
Unknown<===>I proceeded, however, to carry it out; but it was nearly six months before I could pull myself and my little fortune out of the place into which we had grown.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins kept me well informed regarding Lattimore affairs; and the _Herald_ followed me home.
Unknown<===>Jim's letters were long typewritten communications, dictated at speed, and mailed, sometimes one a day, at other times at intervals of weeks.
Unknown<===>"This is a sure-enough 'winter of our discontent,'" one of these letters runs, "but the scope of our operations will widen as the frost comes out of the ground.
Unknown<===>We're now confined to the psychical field.
Unknown<===>Subjectively speaking, though, the plot thickens.
Unknown<===>Captain Tolliver is in the secondary stages of real-estate dementia, and spreads the contagion daily.
Unknown<===>There's no quarantine regulation to cover the case, and Lattimore seems doomed to the acme of prosperity.
Unknown<===>This is the age of great cities, saith the Captain, and that Lattimore is not already a town of 150,000 people is one of the strangest, one of the most inexplicable things in the world, in view of the distance we are lag of the country about us, so far as development is concerned.
Unknown<===>And as our beginning has been tardy, so will our progress be rapid, even as waters long dammed up rush out to devour the plains, etc.
Unknown<===>, etc.
Unknown<===>"In this we are all agreed.
Unknown<===>We want a good, steady, natural growth--and no boom.
Unknown<===>"When a boom recognizes itself as such, it's all over, and the stuff off.
Unknown<===>The time for letting go of a great wheel is when it starts down hill.
Unknown<===>But our wheels are all going up--even if they are all in our heads, as yet.
Unknown<===>"You will remember the railway connection of which I spoke to you.
Unknown<===>Well, that thing has assumed, all of a sudden, a concreteness as welcome as it is unexpected.
Unknown<===>Ballard showed me a telegram yesterday from lower Broadway (the heart of Darkest N.
Unknown<===>Y.
Unknown<===>) which tends to prove that people there are ready to finance the deal.
Unknown<===>It would have amused you to see the horizontality of the coat-tails of the management of the Lattimore & Great Western, as they flaxed round getting up a directors' meeting, so as to have a real, live directorate of this great transcontinental line for the wolves of Wall Street to do business with.
Unknown<===>Things like this are what you miss by hibernating there, instead of dropping everything and applying here for your pro rata share of the gayety of nations and the concomitant scads.
Unknown<===>"I was elected president of the road, and as soon as we get a little track, and an engine, I expect to obtain an exchange of passes with all my fellow monopolists in North America.
Unknown<===>I at once fired back an answer to Ballard's telegram, which must have produced an impression upon the Gould and Vanderbilt interests--if they got wind of it.
Unknown<===>If the L.
Unknown<===>& G.
Unknown<===>W.
Unknown<===>should pass the paper stage next summer, it will do a whole lot towards carrying this burg beyond the hypnotic period of development.
Unknown<===>"The Angus Falls branch is going to build in next summer, I am confident, and that means another division headquarters and, probably, machine-shops.
Unknown<===>I'm working with some of the trilobites here to form a pool, and offer the company grounds for additional yards and a roundhouse and shops.
Unknown<===>Captain Tolliver interviewed General Lattimore about it, and got turned down.
Unknown<===>"'He told me, suh,' reported the Captain, in a fine white passion, 'that if any railway system desiahs to come to Lattimore, it has his puhmission.
Unknown<===>That the Injuns didn't give him any bonus when he came; and that he had to build his own houses and yahds, by gad, at his own expense, and defend 'em, too, and that if any railroad was thinkin' of comin' hyah, it was doubtless because it was good business fo' 'em to come; and that if they wanted any of his land, were willing to pay him his price, there wouldn't be any difficulty about theiah getting it.
Unknown<===>And that if there should arise any difference, which he should deeply regret, but would try to live through, the powah of eminent domain with which railways ah clothed will enable the company to get what land is necessary by legal means.
Unknown<===>"'I could take these observations,' said the Captain, 'as nothing except a gratuitous insult to one who approached him, suh, in a spirit of pure benevolence and civic patriotism.
Unknown<===>It shows the kind of tyrants who commanded the oppressors of the South, suh.
Unknown<===>Only his gray hairs protected him, suh, only his gray hairs.
Unknown<===>'"  "It's a little hard to separate the General from the Captain, in this report of the committee on railway extensions," said my wife.
Unknown<===>"The only thing that's clear about it," said I, "is that Jim is having a good deal of fun with the Captain.
Unknown<===>"  This became clearer as the correspondence went on.
Unknown<===>"Tolliver thinks," said he, in another letter, "that the Angus Falls extension can be pulled through.
Unknown<===>However, I recall that only yesterday the Captain, in private, denounced the citizens of Lattimore as beneath the contempt of gentlemen of breadth of view.
Unknown<===>'I shall dispose of my holdin's hyah,' said he, with a stately sweep indicative of their extent, 'at any sacrifice, and depaht, cuhsin' the day I devoted myself to the redemption of such cattle.
Unknown<===>'  "But, at that particular moment, he had just failed in an attempt to sell Bill Trescott a bunch of choice outlying gold bricks, and was somewhat heated with wine.
Unknown<===>This to the haughty Southron was ample excuse for confiding to me the round, unvarnished truth about us mudsills.
Unknown<===>"Josie and I often talk of you and your wife.
Unknown<===>I don't know what I'd do out here if it weren't for Josie.
Unknown<===>She refuses to enthuse over our 'natural, healthy growth,' which we look for; but I guess that's because she doesn't care for the things that the rest of us are striving for.
Unknown<===>But she's the only person here with whom one can really converse.
Unknown<===>You'd be astonished to see how pretty she is in her furs, and set like a jewel in my new sleigh; but I'm becoming keenly aware of the fact.
Unknown<===>"  We were afterwards told that the trilobites had shaken off their fossilhood, and that the Angus Falls extension, with the engine-house and machine-shops, had been "landed.
Unknown<===>"  "This," he wrote, "means enough new families to make a noticeable increase in our population.
Unknown<===>Things will be popping here soon.
Unknown<===>Come on and help shake the popper; hurry up with your moving, or it will all be over, including the shouting.
Unknown<===>"  We were not entirely dependent upon Jim's letters for Lattimore news.
Unknown<===>Mrs.
Unknown<===>Barslow kept up a desultory correspondence with Miss Trescott, begun upon some pretext and continued upon none at all.
Unknown<===>In one of these letters Josie (for so we soon learned to call her) wrote:  "Our little town is changing so that it no longer seems familiar.
Unknown<===>Not that the change is visible.
Unknown<===>Beyond an unusual number of strangers or recent comers, there is nothing new to strike the eye.
Unknown<===>But the talk everywhere is of a new railroad and other improvements.
Unknown<===>One needs only to shut one's eyes and listen, to imagine that the town is already a real city.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins seems to be the center of this new civic self-esteem.
Unknown<===>The air is full of it, and I admit that I am affected by it.
Unknown<===>I have      "'A feeling, as when eager crowds await,     Before a palace gate,     Some wondrous pageant.
Unknown<===>'  "You are indebted to Captain Tolliver for the quotation, and to Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins for the idea.
Unknown<===>The Captain induced me to read the book in which I found the lines.
Unknown<===>He stigmatizes the preference given to the Northern poets--Longfellow, for instance--over Timrod as 'the crowning infamy of American letters.
Unknown<===>' He has taken the trouble to lay out a course of study for me, the object of which is to place me right in my appreciation of the literary men of the South.
Unknown<===>It includes Pollard's 'Lost Cause' and the works of W.
Unknown<===>G.
Unknown<===>Simms.
Unknown<===>I have not fully promised to follow it to the end.
Unknown<===>Timrod, however, is a treat.
Unknown<===>"  That last quiet winter will always be set apart in my memory, as a time like no other.
Unknown<===>It was a sitting down on a milestone to rest.
Unknown<===>Back of us lay the busy past--busy with trivial things, it seemed to me, but full of varied activity nevertheless.
Unknown<===>A boy will desire mightily to finish a cob-house; and when it is done he will smilingly knock it about the barn floor.
Unknown<===>So I was tearing down and leaving the fabric of relationship which I had once prized so highly.
Unknown<===>The life upon which I expected to enter promised well.
Unknown<===>In fact, to a man of medium ability, only, and no training in large affairs, it promised exceedingly well.
Unknown<===>I knew that Jim was strong, and that his old regard for me had taken new life and a firm hold upon him.
Unknown<===>But when, removed from his immediate influence, I looked the situation in the face, the future loomed so mysteriously bizarre that I shrank from it.
Unknown<===>All his skimble-skamble talk about psychology and hypnotism, and that other rambling discourse of pirate caves and buccaneering cruises, made me feel sometimes as if I were about to form a partnership with Aladdin, or the King of the Golden Mountain.
Unknown<===>If he had asked me, merely, to come to Lattimore and go into the real estate and insurance business with him, I am sure I should have had none of this mental vertigo.
Unknown<===>Yet what more had he done.
Unknown<===>As to the boom, I had, as yet, not a particle of objective confidence in it; but, subconsciously, I felt, as did the town "doomed to prosperity," a sense of impending events.
Unknown<===>In spite of some presentiments and doubts, it was, on the whole, with high hopes that we, on an aguish spring day, reached Lattimore with our stuff (as the Scriptures term it), and knew that, for weal or woe, it was our home.
Unknown<===>Jim was again at the station to meet us, and seemed delighted at our arrival.
Unknown<===>I thought I saw some sort of absent-mindedness or absorbedness in his manner, so that he seemed hardly like himself.
Unknown<===>Josie was there with him, and while she and Alice were greeting each other, I saw Jim scanning the little crowd at the station as if for some other arrival.
Unknown<===>At last, his eye told me that whatever it was for which he was looking, he had found it; and I followed his glance.
Unknown<===>It rested on the last person to alight from the train--a tall, sinewy, soldierly-built youngish man, who wore an overcoat of black, falling away in front, so as to reveal a black frock coat tightly buttoned up and a snowy shirt-front with a glittering gem sparkling from the center of it.
Unknown<===>On his head was a shining silk hat--a thing so rare in that community as to be noticeable, and to stamp the wearer as an outsider.
Unknown<===>His beard was clipped close, and at the chin ran out into a pronounced Vandyke point.
Unknown<===>His mustaches were black, heavy, and waxed.
Unknown<===>His whole external appearance betokened wealth, and he exuded mystery.
Unknown<===>He had not taken two steps from the car before the people on the platform were standing on tiptoe to see him.
Unknown<===>"Bus to the Centropolis.
Unknown<===>" queried the driver of the omnibus.
Unknown<===>The stranger looked at the conveyance, filled as it was with a load of traveling men and casuals; and, frowning darkly, turned to the negro who accompanied him, saying, "Haven't you any carriage here, Pearson.
Unknown<===>"  "Yes, sah," responded the servant, pointing to a closed vehicle.
Unknown<===>"Right hyah, sah.
Unknown<===>"  My wife stood looking, with a little amused smile, at the picturesque group, so out of the ordinary at the time and place.
Unknown<===>Miss Trescott was gazing intently at the stranger, and at the moment when he spoke she clutched my wife's arm so tightly as to startle her.
Unknown<===>I heard Alice make some inquiry as to the cause of her agitation, and as I looked at her, I could see in the one glance her face, gone suddenly white as death, and the dark visage of the tall stranger.
Unknown<===>And it seemed to me as if I had seen the same thing before.
Unknown<===>Then, the negro pointing the way to the closed carriage, the group separated to left and right, the stranger passed through to the carriage, and the picture, and with it my odd mental impression, dissolved.
Unknown<===>The negro lifted two or three heavy bags to the coachman, gave the transfer man some baggage-checks, and the equipage moved away toward the hotel.
Unknown<===>All this took place in a moment, during which the usual transactions on the platform were suspended.
Unknown<===>The conductor failed to give the usual signal for the departure of the train.
Unknown<===>The engineer leaned from the cab and gazed.
Unknown<===>Jim's eye rested on the stranger and his servant for an instant only; but during that time he seemed to take an observation, come to a conclusion, and dismiss the whole matter.
Unknown<===>"Here, John," said he to the drayman, "take these trunks to the Centropolis.
Unknown<===>We'd like 'em this week, too.
Unknown<===>None of that old trick of yours of dumping 'em in the crick, you know.
Unknown<===>"  "They'll be up there in five minutes all right, Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins," said John, grinning at Jim's allusion to some accident, the knowledge of which appeared to be confined to himself and Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins, and to constitute a bond of sympathy between them.
Unknown<===>Jim turned to us with redoubled heartiness, all his absent-mindedness gone.
Unknown<===>"I'll drive you to the hotel," said Jim.
Unknown<===>"You'll--"  "Miss Trescott is ill--" said Alice.
Unknown<===>"Not at all," said Josie; "it has passed entirely.
Unknown<===>Only, when you have taken Mr.
Unknown<===>and Mrs.
Unknown<===>Barslow to the hotel, will you please take me home.
Unknown<===>Our little supper-party--I don't feel quite equal to it, if you will excuse me.
Unknown<===>"     CHAPTER VIII.
Unknown<===>A Welcome to Wall Street and Us.
Unknown<===>"Welcome.
Unknown<===>" intoned Captain Tolliver, with his hat in his hand, bowing low to Mrs.
Unknown<===>Barslow.
Unknown<===>"Welcome, Madam and suh, in the capacity of Lattimoreans.
Unknown<===>That we shall be the bettah fo' yo' residence among us the' can be no doubt.
Unknown<===>That you will be prospahed beyond yo' wildest dreams I believe equally cehtain.
Unknown<===>Welcome.
Unknown<===>"  This address was delivered within thirty seconds of the time of our arrival at our old rooms in the Centropolis.
Unknown<===>The Captain saluted us in a manner extravagantly polite, mysteriously enthusiastic.
Unknown<===>The air of mystery was deepened when he called again to see Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins in the evening and was invited in.
Unknown<===>"Did you-all notice that distinguished and opulent-looking gentleman who got off the train this evening.
Unknown<===>" said he in a stage whisper.
Unknown<===>"Mahk my words, the coming of such men, _his_ coming, is fraught with the deepest significance to us all.
Unknown<===>All my holdin's ah withdrawn from mahket until fu'the' developments.
Unknown<===>"  "Seems to travel in style," said Jim; "all sorts of good clothes, colored body-servant, closed carriage ordered by wire--it does look juicy, don't it, now.
Unknown<===>"  "He has the entiah second flo' front suite.
Unknown<===>The niggah has already sent out fo' a bahbah," said the Captain.
Unknown<===>"Lattimore has at last attracted the notice of adequate capital, and will now assume huh true place in the bright galaxy of American cities.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Barslow, I shall ask puhmission to call upon you in the mo'nin' with reference to a project which will make the fo'tunes of a dozen men, and that within the next ninety days.
Unknown<===>Good evenin', suh; good evenin', Madam.
Unknown<===>I feel that you have come among us at a propitious moment.
Unknown<===>"  "The Captain merely hints at the truth which struggles in him for utterance," said Jim.
Unknown<===>"I prove this by informing you that I couldn't get you a house.
Unknown<===>This shows, too, that the census returns are a calumny upon Lattimore.
Unknown<===>You'll have to stay at the Centropolis until something turns up or you can build.
Unknown<===>"  "Oh, dear.
Unknown<===>" said Alice.
Unknown<===>"Hotel life isn't living at all.
Unknown<===>I hope it won't be long.
Unknown<===>"  "It will have its advantages for Al," said Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins.
Unknown<===>"This financial maelstrom, which will draw everything to Lattimore, will have its core right in this hotel--a mighty good place to be.
Unknown<===>Things of all kinds have been floating about in the air for months; the precipitation is beginning now.
Unknown<===>The psychological moment has arrived--you have brought it with you, Mrs.
Unknown<===>Barslow.
Unknown<===>The moon-flower of Lattimore's 'gradual, healthy growth' is going to burst, and that right soon.
Unknown<===>"  "Has Captain Tolliver infected you.
Unknown<===>" inquired Alice.
Unknown<===>"He told us the same thing, with less of tropes and figures.
Unknown<===>"  "On any still morning," said Jim, "you can hear the wheels go round in the Captain's head; but his instinct for real-estate conditions is as accurate as a pocket-gopher's.
Unknown<===>The Captain, in a hysterical sort of way, is right: I consider that a cinch.
Unknown<===>Good-night, friends, and pleasant dreams.
Unknown<===>I expect to see you at breakfast; but if I shouldn't, Al, you'll come aboard at nine, won't you, and help run up the Jolly Roger.
Unknown<===>I think I smell pieces-of-eight in the air.
Unknown<===>And, by the way, Miss Trescott says for me to assure you that her vertigo, which she had for the first time in her life, is gone, and she never felt better.
Unknown<===>"  As Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins passed from our parlor, he let in a bell-boy with the card of Mr.
Unknown<===>Clifford Giddings, representing the Lattimore Morning _Herald_.
Unknown<===>"See him down in the lobby," said Alice.
Unknown<===>"I want a story," said he as we met, "on the city and its future.
Unknown<===>The _Herald_ readers will be glad of anything from Mr.
Unknown<===>Barslow, whose coming they have so long looked forward to, as intimately connected with the city's development.
Unknown<===>"  "My dear sir," I replied, somewhat astonished at the importance which he was pleased to attach to my arrival, "abstractly, my removal to Lattimore is my best testimony on that; concretely, I ought to ask information of you.
Unknown<===>"  We sat down in a corner of the lobby, our chairs side by side, facing opposite ways.
Unknown<===>He lighted a cigar, and gave me one.
Unknown<===>In looks he was young; in behavior he had the self-possession and poise of maturity.
Unknown<===>He wore a long mackintosh which sparkled with mist.
Unknown<===>His slouch hat looked new and was carefully dinted.
Unknown<===>His dress was almost natty in an unconventional way, and his manners accorded with his garb.
Unknown<===>He acted as if for years we had casually met daily.
Unknown<===>His tone and attitude evinced respect, was entirely free from presumption, equally devoid of reserve, carried with it no hint of familiarity, but assumed a perfect understanding.
Unknown<===>The barrier which usually keeps strangers apart he neither broke down, which must have been offensive, nor overleaped, which would have been presumptuous.
Unknown<===>He covered it with that demeanor of his, and together we sat down upon it.
Unknown<===>"I thought the _Herald_ was an evening paper," said I.
Unknown<===>"It was, in the days of yore," he replied; "but Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins happened to see me in Chicago one day, and advised me to come out and look the old thing over with a view to purchasing the plant.
Unknown<===>You observe the result.
Unknown<===>As fellow immigrants, I hope there will be a bond of sympathy between us.
Unknown<===>You think, of course, that Lattimore is a coming city.
Unknown<===>"  "Yes.
Unknown<===>"  "Its geographical situation seems to render its development inevitable, doesn't it.
Unknown<===>And," he went on, "the railway conditions seem peculiarly promising just now.
Unknown<===>"  "Yes," said I, "but the natural resources of the city and the surrounding country appeal most strongly to me.
Unknown<===>"  "They are certainly very exceptional, aren't they.
Unknown<===>" said he, as if the matter had never occurred to him before.
Unknown<===>Then he went on telling me things, more than asking questions, about the jobbing trades, the brick and tile and associated industries, the cement factory, which he spoke of as if actually _in esse_, the projected elevators, the flouring-mills, and finally returned to railway matters.
Unknown<===>"What is your opinion of the Lattimore & Great Western, Mr.
Unknown<===>Barslow.
Unknown<===>" he asked.
Unknown<===>"I cannot say that I have any," I answered, "except that its construction would bring great good to Lattimore.
Unknown<===>"  "It could scarcely fail," said he, "to bring in two or three systems which we now lack, could it.
Unknown<===>"  I very sincerely said that I did not know.
Unknown<===>After a few more questions concerning our plans for the future, Mr.
Unknown<===>Giddings vanished into the night, silently, as an autumn leaf parting from its bough.
Unknown<===>I thought of him no more until I unfolded the _Herald_ in the morning as we sat at breakfast, and saw that my interview was made a feature of the day's news.
Unknown<===>"Mr.
Unknown<===>Albert F.
Unknown<===>Barslow," it read, "of the firm of Elkins & Barslow, is stopping at the Centropolis.
Unknown<===>He arrived by the 6:15 train last evening, and with his family has taken a suite of rooms pending the erection of a residence.
Unknown<===>They have not definitely decided as to the location of their new home; but it may confidently be stated that they will build something which will be a notable addition to the architectural beauties of Lattimore--already proud of her title, the City of Homes.
Unknown<===>"  "I am very glad to know about this," said Alice.
Unknown<===>"Your man Giddings has nerve, whatever else he may lack," said I to the smiling Elkins across the table.
Unknown<===>"Am I obliged to make good all these representations.
Unknown<===>I ask, that I may know the rules of the game, merely.
Unknown<===>"  "One rule is that you mustn't deny any accusations of future magnificence, for two reasons: they may come true, and they help things on.
Unknown<===>You are supposed to have left your modesty in cold storage somewhere.
Unknown<===>Read on.
Unknown<===>"  "Mr.
Unknown<===>Barslow," I read, "has long been a most potent political factor in his native state, but is, first of all, a business man.
Unknown<===>He brings his charming young wife--"  "Really, a most discriminating journalist," interjected Alice.
Unknown<===>"--and social circles, as well as the business world, will find them a most desirable accession to Lattimore's population.
Unknown<===>"  "Why this is absolute, slavish devotion to facts," said Jim; "where does the word-painting come in.
Unknown<===>"  "Here it is," said I.
Unknown<===>"Mr.
Unknown<===>Barslow is some years under middle age, and looks the intense modern business man in every feature.
Unknown<===>His mind seems to have already become saturated with the conception of the enormous possibilities of Lattimore.
Unknown<===>He impresses those who have met him as one of the few men capable of pulling his share in double harness with James R.
Unknown<===>Elkins.
Unknown<===>"  "The fellow piles it on a little strong at times, doesn't he, Mrs.
Unknown<===>Barslow.
Unknown<===>" said Jim.
Unknown<===>"He brings to our city," I read on, "his vigorous mind, his fortune, and a determination never to rest until the city passes the 100,000 mark.
Unknown<===>To a _Herald_ representative, last night, he spoke strongly and eloquently of our great natural resources.
Unknown<===>"  Then followed a skillfully handled expansion of our _tete-a-tete_ talk in the lobby.
Unknown<===>"Mr.
Unknown<===>Barslow," the report went on, "very courteously declined to discuss the L.
Unknown<===>& G.
Unknown<===>W.
Unknown<===>situation.
Unknown<===>It seems evident, however, from remarks dropped by him, that he regards the construction of this road as inevitable, and as a project which, successfully carried out, cannot fail to make Lattimore the point to which all the Western and Southwestern systems of railways must converge.
Unknown<===>"  "You're doing it like a veteran.
Unknown<===>" cried Jim.
Unknown<===>"Admirable.
Unknown<===>Just the proper infusion of mystery; I couldn't have done better myself.
Unknown<===>"  "Credit it all to Giddings," I protested.
Unknown<===>"And note that the center of the stage is reserved to our mysterious fellow lodger and co-arrival.
Unknown<===>"  "Yes, I saw that," said Jim.
Unknown<===>"Isn't Giddings a peach.
Unknown<===>Let Mrs.
Unknown<===>Barslow hear it.
Unknown<===>"  "She ought to be able to hear these headlines," said I, "without any reading: 'J.
Unknown<===>Bedford Cornish arrives.
Unknown<===>Wall Street's Millions On the Ground in the Person of One of Her Great Financiers.
Unknown<===>Bull Movement in Real Estate Noted Last Night.
Unknown<===>Does He Represent the Great Railway Interests.
Unknown<===>'"  "Real estate and financial circles," ran the article under these headlines, "are thrown into something of a fever by the arrival, on the 6:15 express last evening, of a gentleman of distinguished appearance, who took five rooms _en suite_ on the second floor of the Centropolis, and registered in a bold hand as J.
Unknown<===>Bedford Cornish, of New York.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish consented to see a _Herald_ representative last night, but was very reticent as to his plans and the objects of his visit.
Unknown<===>He simply says that he represents capital seeking investment.
Unknown<===>He would not admit that he is connected with any of the great railway interests, or that his visit has any relation to the building of the Lattimore & Great Western.
Unknown<===>The _Herald_ is able to say, however, that its New York correspondent informs it that Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish is a member of the firm of Lusch, Carskaddan & Mayer, of Wall Street.
Unknown<===>This firm is well known as one of the concerns handling large amounts of European capital, and said to be intimately associated with the Rothschilds.
Unknown<===>Financial journals have recently noted the fact that these concerns are becoming embarrassed by the plethora of funds seeking investment, and are turning their attention to the development of railway systems and cities in the United States.
Unknown<===>Their South American and Australian investments have not proven satisfactory, especially the former, owing to the character of the people of Latin America.
Unknown<===>It has been pointed out that no real-estate investment can be more than moderately profitable in climates which render the people content with a mere living, and that the restless and unsatisfied vigor of the Anglo-Saxon alone can make lands and railways permanently remunerative.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish admitted these facts when they were pointed out to him, and immediately changed the subject.
Unknown<===>"Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish is a very handsome and opulent-looking gentleman, and seems to live in a style somewhat luxurious for the Occident.
Unknown<===>He has a colored body-servant, who seems to reflect the mystery of his master; but if he has any other reflections, the _Herald_ is none the wiser for them.
Unknown<===>Admittance to the suite of rooms was obtained by sending in the reporter's card, which vanished into a sybaritic gloom, borne on a golden salver.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish seems to be very exclusive, his meals being served in his rooms; and even his barber has instructions to call upon him each morning.
Unknown<===>One wonders why the barber is called in so frequently, until one marks the smooth-shaven cheeks above the close-clipped, pointed, black, Vandyke beard.
Unknown<===>He is withal very cordial and courtly in his manners.
Unknown<===>"James R.
Unknown<===>Elkins, when seen last evening, refused to talk, except to say that, in financial circles, it has been known for some days that important developments may be now momently expected, and that some such thing as the visit of Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish was imminent.
Unknown<===>Captain Marion Tolliver expressed himself freely, and to the effect that this mysterious visit is of the utmost importance to Lattimore, and a thing of national if not world-wide importance.
Unknown<===>"  "Now, that justifies my confidence in Giddings," said Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins, "fulfilling at the same time the requirements of journalism and hypnotism.
Unknown<===>Come, Al, our bark is on the sea, our boat is on the shore.
Unknown<===>The Spanish galleons are even now hiding in the tall grass, in expectation of our cruise.
Unknown<===>Let us hence to the office.
Unknown<===>"     CHAPTER IX.
Unknown<===>I Go Aboard and We Unfurl the Jolly Roger.
Unknown<===>"We must act, and act at once.
Unknown<===>" said the Captain, his voice thrilling with intensity.
Unknown<===>"This piece of property will be gone befo' night.
Unknown<===>All it takes is a paltry three thousand dolla's, and within ninety days--no man can say what its value will be.
Unknown<===>We can plat it, and within ten days we may have ouah money back.
Unknown<===>Allow me to draw on you fo' three thou--"  "But," said I, "I can make no move in such a matter at this time without conference with Mr.
Unknown<===>--"  "Very well, suh, very well.
Unknown<===>" said the Captain, regarding me with a look that showed how much better things he had expected of me.
Unknown<===>"Opportunity, suh, knocks once--By the way, excuse me, suh.
Unknown<===>"  And he darted from the office, took the trail of Mr.
Unknown<===>Macdonald, whom he had seen passing, brought him to bay in front of the post-office, and dragged him away to some doom, the nature of which I could only surmise.
Unknown<===>This took place on the morning of my first day with Elkins & Barslow.
Unknown<===>I was to take up the office work.
Unknown<===>"That will be easy for you from the first," said Jim.
Unknown<===>"Your experience as rob-ee down there in Posey County makes you a sort of specialist in that sort of thing; and pretty soon all other things shall be added unto it.
Unknown<===>"  The Captain's onslaught in the first half-hour admonished me that a good deal was already added to it.
Unknown<===>On that very day, too, we had our first conference with Mr.
Unknown<===>Hinckley.
Unknown<===>We wanted to handle securities, said Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins, and should have a great many of them, and that was quite in Mr.
Unknown<===>Hinckley's line.
Unknown<===>To carry them ourselves would soon absorb all our capital.
Unknown<===>We must liberate it by floating the commercial paper which we took in.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Hinckley's bank was known to be strong, his standing was of the highest, and a trust company in alliance with him could not fail to find a good market for its paper.
Unknown<===>With an old banker's timidity, Hinckley seemed to hesitate; yet the prospects seemed so good that I felt that this consent was sure to be given.
Unknown<===>Jim courted him assiduously, and the intimacy between him and the Hinckley family became noticeable.
Unknown<===>"Jim," said I, one day, "you have an unerring eye for the pleasant things of life.
Unknown<===>I couldn't help thinking of this to-day when I saw you for the twentieth time spinning along the street in Miss Hinckley's carriage, beside its owner.
Unknown<===>She's one of the handsomest girls, in her flaxen-haired way, that I know of.
Unknown<===>"  "Isn't she a study in curves and pink and white.
Unknown<===>" said Jim.
Unknown<===>"And she understands this trust company business as well as her father.
Unknown<===>"  The trust company's stock, he went on to explain, ignoring Antonia, seemed to be already oversubscribed.
Unknown<===>Our firm, Hinckley, and Jim's Chicago and New York friends, including Harper, all stood ready to take blocks of it, and there was no reason for requiring Hinckley to put much actual money in for this.
Unknown<===>He could pay for it out of his profits soon, and make a fortune without any outlay.
Unknown<===>Good credit was the prime necessity, and that Mr.
Unknown<===>Hinckley certainly had.
Unknown<===>So the celebrated Grain Belt Trust Company was begun--a name about which such mighty interests were to cluster, that I know I should have shrunk from the responsibility had I known what a gigantic thing we were creating.
Unknown<===>As the days wore on, Captain Tolliver's dementia spread and raged virulently.
Unknown<===>The dark-visaged Cornish, with his air of mystery, his habits so at odds with the society of Lattimore, was in the very focus of attention.
Unknown<===>For a day or so, the effect which Mr.
Unknown<===>Giddings's report attributed to his invasion failed to disclose itself to me.
Unknown<===>Then the delirium became manifest, and swept over the town like a were-wolf delusion through a medieval village.
Unknown<===>Its immediate occasion seemed to be a group of real-estate conveyances, announced in the _Herald_ one morning, surpassing in importance anything in the history of the town.
Unknown<===>Some of the lands transferred were acreage; some were waste and vacant tracts along Brushy Creek and the river; one piece was a suburban farm; but the mass of it was along Main Street and in the business district.
Unknown<===>The grantees were for the most part strange names in Lattimore, some individuals, some corporations.
Unknown<===>All the sales were at prices hitherto unknown.
Unknown<===>It was to be remarked, too, that in most cases the property had been purchased not long before, by some of the group of newer comers and at the old modest prices.
Unknown<===>Our firm seemed to have profited heavily in these transactions, as had Captain Tolliver also.
Unknown<===>We of the "new crowd" had begun our mock-trading to "establish the market.
Unknown<===>" Prices were going up, up; and all one had to do was to buy to-day and sell to-morrow.
Unknown<===>Real values, for actual use, seemed to be forgotten.
Unknown<===>The most memorable moment in this first, acutest stage in our development was one bright day, within a week or so of our coming.
Unknown<===>The lawns were taking on their summer emerald, robins were piping in the maples, and down in the cottonwoods and lindens on the river front crows and jays were jargoning their immemorial and cheery lingo.
Unknown<===>Surveyors were running lines and making plats in the suburbs, peeped at by gophers, and greeted by the roundelays of meadow-larks.
Unknown<===>But on the street-corners, in the offices of lawyers and real-estate agents, and in the lobbies of the hotels, the trading was lively.
Unknown<===>Then for the first time the influx of real buyers from the outside became noticeable.
Unknown<===>The landlord of the Centropolis could scarcely care for his guests.
Unknown<===>They talked of blocks, quarter-blocks, and the choice acreage they had bought, and of the profits they had made in this and other cities and towns (where this same speculative fever was epidemic), until Alice fled to the Trescott farm--as she said, to avoid the mixture of real estate with her meals.
Unknown<===>The telegraph offices were gorged with messages to non-resident property owners, begging for prices on good inside lots.
Unknown<===>Staid, slow-going lot-owners, who had grown old in patiently paying taxes on patches of dog-fennel and sand-burrs, dazedly vacillated between acceptance and rejection of tempting propositions, dreading the missing of the chance so long awaited, fearing misjudgment as to the height of the wave, dreading a future of regret at having sold too low.
Unknown<===>One of these, an old woman, toothless and bent, hobbled to our office and asked for Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins.
Unknown<===>He was busy, and so I received her.
Unknown<===>"It's about that quarter-block with the Donegal ruin on it," said Jim; "the one I showed you yesterday.
Unknown<===>Offer her five thousand, one-fourth down, balance in one, two, and three years, eight per cent.
Unknown<===>"  "I wanted to ask Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins about me home," said she.
Unknown<===>"I tuk in washin' to buy it, an' me son, poor Patsy, God rist 'is soul, he helped wid th' bit of money from the Brotherhood, whin he was kilt betune the cars.
Unknown<===>It was sivin hundred an' fifty dollars, an' now Thronson offers me four thousan'.
Unknown<===>I told him I'd sell, fer it's a fortune for a workin' woman; but befure I signed papers, I wanted to ask Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins; he's such a fair-spoken man, an' knowin' to me min-folks in Peoria.
Unknown<===>"  "If you want to sell, Mrs.
Unknown<===>Collins," said I, "we will take your property at five thousand dollars.
Unknown<===>"  She started, and regarded me, first in amazement, then with distrust, shading off into hostility.
Unknown<===>"Thank ye kindly, sir," said she; "I'll be goin' now.
Unknown<===>I've med up me moind, if that bit of land is wort all that money t' yees, it's wort more to me.
Unknown<===>Thank ye kindly.
Unknown<===>" and she fled from the presence of the tempter.
Unknown<===>"The town is full of Biddy Collinses," commented Jim.
Unknown<===>"Well, we can't land everything, and couldn't handle the catch if we did.
Unknown<===>In fact, for present purposes, isn't it better to have her refuse.
Unknown<===>"  This incident was the hint upon which our "Syndicate," as it came to be called, acted from time to time, in making fabulous offers to every Biddy Collins in town.
Unknown<===>"Offer twenty thousand," Jim would say.
Unknown<===>"The more you bid the less apt is he to accept; he's a Biddy Collins.
Unknown<===>" And whatever Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins advised was done.
Unknown<===>There were eight or ten of us in the "Syndicate," dubbed by Jim "The Crew," among whom were Tolliver, Macdonald, and Will Lattimore.
Unknown<===>But the inner circle, now drawing closer and closer together, were Elkins, our ruling spirit; Hinckley, our great force in the banking world; and myself.
Unknown<===>Soon, I was given to understand, Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish was to take his place as one of us.
Unknown<===>He and Jim had long known each other, and Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins had the utmost confidence in Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish's usefulness in what he called "the thought-transference department.
Unknown<===>"  Elkins & Barslow kept their offices open night and day, almost, and the number of typewriters and bookkeepers grew astoundingly.
Unknown<===>I became almost a stranger to my wife.
Unknown<===>I got hurried glimpses of Miss Trescott and her mother at the hotel, and knew that she and Alice were becoming fast friends; but so far the social prominence which the _Herald_ had predicted for us had failed to arrive.
Unknown<===>This, to be sure, was our own fault.
Unknown<===>Miss Addison soon gave us up as not available for the church and Sunday-school functions to which she devoted herself.
Unknown<===>Her family connections would have made her _the_ social leader had it not been for the severity of her views and her assumption of the character of the devotee--in spite of which she protestingly went almost everywhere.
Unknown<===>Antonia Hinckley, however, was frankly fond of a good time, and with her dashing and almost hoydenish character easily took the leadership from Miss Addison; and Miss Hinckley sought diligently for means by which we could be properly launched.
Unknown<===>As I left the office one day, a voice from the curb called my name.
Unknown<===>It was Miss Hinckley in a smart trap, to which was harnessed a beautiful horse, standard bred, one could see at a glance.
Unknown<===>I obeyed the summons, and stepped beside the equipage.
Unknown<===>"I want to scold you," said she.
Unknown<===>"Society is being defrauded of the good things which your coming promised.
Unknown<===>Have you taken a vow of seclusion, or what.
Unknown<===>"  "I've been spinning about in the maelstrom of business," I replied.
Unknown<===>"But do not be uneasy; some time we shall take up the matter of inflicting ourselves, and pursue it as vigorously as we now follow our vocation.
Unknown<===>"  "Wouldn't you like to get into the trap, and take a spin of another sort.
Unknown<===>" said she.
Unknown<===>"I'll deposit you safely with Mrs.
Unknown<===>Barslow in time for tea.
Unknown<===>"  I got in, glad of the drive, and for ten minutes her horse was sent at such a pace that conversation was difficult.
Unknown<===>Then he was slowed down to a walk, his head toward home.
Unknown<===>We chatted of casual things--the scenery, the horse, the splendid color of the sunset.
Unknown<===>I was becoming interested in her.
Unknown<===>"I had almost forgotten that there were such things in Lattimore," said I, referring to the topics of our talk.
Unknown<===>"I have become so saturated with lands and lots.
Unknown<===>"  "I don't know much about business," said she, "and I think I'll improve my opportunity by learning something.
Unknown<===>And, first, aren't men sometimes losers by the dishonesty of those who act for them--agents, they are called, aren't they.
Unknown<===>"  Such, I admitted, was unfortunately the case.
Unknown<===>"I should be sorry for--any one I liked--to be injured in such a way.
Unknown<===>Now you must understand how the things you men are interested in permeate the society of us women.
Unknown<===>Why, mamma has almost forgotten the enslavement of our sex, in these new things which have changed our old town so much; so you mustn't wonder if I have heard something of a purely business nature.
Unknown<===>I heard that Captain Tolliver was about to sell Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins the land where the old foundry is, over there, for twenty thousand dollars.
Unknown<===>Now, papa says it isn't worth it; and I know--Sadie Allen and I were in school together, and she comes over from Fairchild several times a year to see me, and I go there, you know; and that land is in her father's estate--I know that the executor has told Captain Tolliver to sell it for ever so much less than that.
Unknown<===>And it seemed so funny, as the Captain was doing the business for both sides--isn't it odd, now.
Unknown<===>"  "It does seem so," said I, "and it is very kind of you.
Unknown<===>I'll talk with Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins about it.
Unknown<===>Please be careful, Miss Hinckley, or you'll drop the wheel in that washout.
Unknown<===>"  She reined up her horse and began speeding him again.
Unknown<===>I could see that this conversation had embarrassed her somehow.
Unknown<===>Her color was high, and her grip of the reins not so steady as at starting.
Unknown<===>This attempt to do Jim a favor was something she considered as of a good deal of consequence.
Unknown<===>I began to note more and more what a really splendid woman she was--tall, fair, her tailor-made gown rounding to the full, firm curves of her figure, her fearless horsemanship hinting at the possession of large and positive traits of character.
Unknown<===>"We women," said she, "might as well abandon all the things commonly known as feminine.
Unknown<===>What good do they do us.
Unknown<===>"  "They gratify your sense of the beautiful," suggested I.
Unknown<===>"You know, Mr.
Unknown<===>Barslow," said she, "that it's not our own sense of the beautiful, mainly, that we seek to gratify; and if the eyes for which they are intended are looking into ledgers and blind to everything except dollar-signs, what's the use.
Unknown<===>"  "Go down to the seashore," said I, "where the people congregate who have nothing to do.
Unknown<===>"  "Not I," said she; "I'll go into real estate, and become as blind as the rest.
Unknown<===>"  Jim paid no attention to my chaffing when I spoke of his conquest, as I called Antonia.
Unknown<===>In fact, he seemed annoyed, and for a long time said nothing.
Unknown<===>"You can see how the Allen estate proposition stands," said he, at last.
Unknown<===>"To let that sell for less than twenty thousand might cost us ten times that amount in lowering the prevailing standard of values.
Unknown<===>The old rule that we should buy in the cheapest market and sell in the dearest is suspended.
Unknown<===>Base is the slave who pays--less than the necessary and proper increase.
Unknown<===>"     CHAPTER X.
Unknown<===>We Dedicate Lynhurst Park.
Unknown<===>The Hindu adept sometimes suspends before the eyes of his subject a bright ball of carnelian or crystal, in the steady contemplation of which the sensitive swims off into the realms of subjectivity--that mysterious bourn from whence no traveler brings anything back.
Unknown<===>J.
Unknown<===>Bedford Cornish was Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins's glittering ball; his psychic subject was the world in general and Lattimore in particular.
Unknown<===>Scientific principles, confirmed by experience, led us to the conclusion that the attitude of fixed contemplation carried with it some nervous strain, ought to be of limited duration, and hence that Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish should remove from our midst the glittering mystery of his presence, lest familiarity should breed contempt.
Unknown<===>So in about ten days he went away, giving to the _Herald_ a parting interview, in which he expressed unbounded delight with Lattimore, and hinted that he might return for a longer stay.
Unknown<===>Editorially, the _Herald_ expressed the hope that this characteristically veiled allusion to a longer sojourn might mean that Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish had some idea of becoming a citizen of Lattimore.
Unknown<===>This would denote, the editorial continued, that men like Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish, accustomed to the mighty world-pulse of New York, could find objects of pursuit equally worthy in Lattimore.
Unknown<===>"Which is mixed metaphor," Mr.
Unknown<===>Giddings admitted in confidence; "but," he continued, "if metaphors, like drinks, happen to be more potent mixed, the _Herald_ proposes to mix 'em.

Unknown<===>"  "I have arrangements made, in my mind, for a sort of al fresco function, to come off about the time Cornish gets back with our London visitor," he replied, "which ought to knit up the ravelled sleeve better than new.
Unknown<===>I'm going to dedicate Lynhurst Park to the nymphs and deities of sport--which wrinkled care derides.
Unknown<===>"  "I hadn't heard of Lynhurst Park," I was forced to say.
Unknown<===>"I'm curious to know, first, who named it, and, second, where it is.
Unknown<===>"  "Didn't I show you those blueprints.
Unknown<===>" he asked.
Unknown<===>"An oversight I assure you.
Unknown<===>As for the scheme, you suggested it yourself that night we first drove out to Trescott's.
Unknown<===>Don't you remember saying something about 'breathing space for the populace'.
Unknown<===>Well, I had the surveys made at once; contracted for the land, all but what Bill owns of it, which we'll have to get later; and had a landscapist out from Chicago to direct us as to what we ought to admire in improving the place.
Unknown<===>As for the name, I'm indebted to kind nature, which planted the valley in basswood, and to Josie, who contributed the philological knowledge and the taste.
Unknown<===>That's the street-car line," said he, unrolling an elaborate plat and pointing.
Unknown<===>"We may throw it over to the west to develop section seven, if we close for it.
Unknown<===>Otherwise, that line is the very thing.
Unknown<===>"  Our street-railway franchise had been granted by the Lattimore city council--they would have granted the public square, had we asked for it in the potent name of "progress"--and Cornish was even now making arrangements for placing our bonds.
Unknown<===>The impossible of less than a year ago was now included in the next season's program, as an inconsiderable feature of a great project for a street-railway system, and the "development" of hundreds of acres of land.
Unknown<===>The place so to be named Lynhurst Park was most agreeably reached by a walk up Brushy Creek from Lattimore.
Unknown<===>Such a stroll took one into the gorge, where the rocks shelved toward each other, until their crowning fringes of cedar almost interlocked, like the eyelashes of drowsiness.
Unknown<===>Down there in the twilight one felt a sense of being defrauded, in contemplation of the fact that the stream was troutless: it was such an ideal place for trout.
Unknown<===>The quiet and mellow gloom made the gorge a favorite trysting-place, and perhaps the cool-blooded stream-folk had fled from the presence of the more fervid dwellers on the banks.
Unknown<===>In the crevices of the rocks were the nests of the village pigeons.
Unknown<===>The combined effects of all these causes was to make this a spot devoted to billing and cooing.
Unknown<===>Farther up the stream the rock walls grew lower and parted wider, islanding a rich bottom of lush grass-plot, alternating with groves of walnut, linden, and elm.
Unknown<===>This was the Lynhurst Park of the blueprints and plats.
Unknown<===>Trescott's farm lay on the right bank, and others on either side; but the houses were none of them near the stream, and the entire walk was wild and woodsy-looking.
Unknown<===>None but nature-lovers came that way.
Unknown<===>Others drove out by the road past Trescott's, seeing more of corn and barn, but less of rock, moss, and fern.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish was to return on Friday with the Honorable De Forest Barr-Smith, who lived in London and "represented English capital.
Unknown<===>" To us Westerners the very hyphen of his name spoke eloquently of L s.
Unknown<===>d.
Unknown<===>Through him we hoped to get the money to build that street railway.
Unknown<===>Cornish had written that Mr.
Unknown<===>Barr-Smith wanted to look the thing over personally; and that, given the element of safety, his people would much prefer an investment of a million to one of ten thousand.
Unknown<===>Cornish further hinted that the London gentleman acted like a man who wanted a side interest in the construction company; as to which he would sound him further by the way.
Unknown<===>"He'll expect something in the way of birds and bottles," observed Elkins; "but they won't mix with the general society of this town, where the worm of the still is popularly supposed to be the original Edenic tempter.
Unknown<===>And he'll want to inspect Lynhurst Park.
Unknown<===>I want him to see our beauty and our chivalry,--meaning the ladies and Captain Tolliver,--and the rest of our best people.
Unknown<===>I guess we'll have to make it a temperate sort of orgy, making up in the spectacular what it lacks in spirituousness.
Unknown<===>"  Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish came, gradually moulting his mystery; but still far above the Lattimore standard in dress and style of living.
Unknown<===>In truth, he always had a good deal of the swell in his make-up, and can almost be acquitted of deceit in the impressions conveyed at his coming.
Unknown<===>The Honorable De Forest Barr-Smith fraternized with Cornish, as he could with no one else.

Unknown<===>Barr-Smith went into the discussion of business propositions freely and confidentially.

Unknown<===>Cornish's unerring conformity of vogue in the manner and as to the occasion of wearing the tuxedo or the claw-hammer coat was clearly restful to Mr.
Unknown<===>Barr-Smith, in this new and strange country, where, if danger was to be avoided, things had to be approached with distended nostril and many preliminary snuffings of the wind.
Unknown<===>There came with these two a younger brother of Mr.
Unknown<===>Barr-Smith, Cecil--a big young civil engineer, just out of college, and as like his brother in accent and dress as could be expected of one of his years; but national characteristics are matters of growth, and college boys all over the world are a good deal alike.
Unknown<===>Cecil Barr-Smith, with his red mustache, his dark eyes, and his six feet of British brawn, was nearer in touch with our younger people that first day than his honorable brother ever became.

Unknown<===>She resembles sister Gritty remarkably; the same complexion and the same style, you know.
Unknown<===>Quite so.
Unknown<===>"  The Lynhurst function was the real introduction of these three gentlemen to Lattimore society.
Unknown<===>I knew nothing of the arrangements, except what I could deduce from Jim's volume of business with caterers and other handicraftsmen; and I looked forward to the fete with much curiosity.
Unknown<===>The weather, that afternoon, made an outing quite the natural thing; for it was hot.
Unknown<===>The ladies in their most summery gowns fluttered like white dryads from shade to shade, uttering bird-like pipings of surprise at the preparations made for their entertainment.
Unknown<===>The ravine had been transformed.
Unknown<===>At an available point in its bed Jim had thrown a dam across the stream, and a beautiful little lake rippled in the breeze, bearing on its bosom a bright-colored boat, which in our ignorance of things Venetian we mistakenly dubbed a gondola.
Unknown<===>At the upper end of this water the canvas of a large pavilion gleamed whitely through the greenery, displaying from its top the British and American flags, their color reflected in a particolored streak on the wimpling face of the lake.
Unknown<===>The groves, in the tops of which the woodpeckers, warblers, and vireos disturbedly carried on the imperatively necessary work of rearing their broods, were gay with festoons of Chinese lanterns in readiness for the evening.
Unknown<===>Hammocks were slung from tree to tree, cushions and seats were arranged in cosy nooks; and when my wife and I stepped from our carriage, all these appliances for the utilization of shade and leisure were in full use.
Unknown<===>The "gondola" was making, trips from the cascade (as the dam was already called) to the pavilion, carrying loads of young people from whom came to our ears those peals of merriment which have everywhere but one meaning, and that a part of the world-old mystery of the way of a man with a maid.
Unknown<===>Jim was on the ground early, to receive the guests and keep the management in hand.

Unknown<===>And when Jim rose to meet his guests, she dismissed him with one of those charmingly inviting glances and gestures with which such an adorable woman spins the thread by which the banished one is drawn back,--and then she disappeared until the dinner was served.

Unknown<===>Barr-Smith on the other hand, was garbed cap-a-pie for an outing, presenting an appearance with which the racket, the bat, or even the alpenstock might have been conjoined in perfect harmony.

Unknown<===>We walked about in the every-day vestments of the shops, banks, and offices, illustrating the difference between a state of society in which apparel is regarded as an incident in life, and one rising to the height of realizing its true significance as a religion.

Unknown<===>Barr-Smith bowed not the knee to the Baal of western clothes-monotone, but daily sent out his sartorial orisons, keeping his windows open toward the Jerusalem of his London tailor, in a manner which would have delighted a Teufelsdroeckh.
Unknown<===>He was a short man, with protruding cheeks, and a nose ending in an amorphous flare of purple and scarlet.
