Unknown<===>"  Mr.
Unknown<===>Barr-Smith, in response to the allusions to him, assured us that the presence of people such as he had had the pleasure of meeting in Lattimore was sufficient in itself to account for the forward movement in the community, which the visitor could not fail to observe.
Unknown<===>"In a state of society where people are not averse to changing their abodes," he said, "and where the social atom, if I may so express myself, is in a state of mobility, the presence of such magnets as our toastmaster, and the other gentlemen to whose courteous remarks I am responding, must draw 'em to themselves, you may be jolly well assured of that.
Unknown<===>And if the gentlemen should fail, the thing which should resist the attractive power of the American ladies must be more fixed in its habits than even the conservative English gentleman, who prides himself upon his stability, er--ah--his taking a position and sticking by it, in spite of the--of anything, you know.
Unknown<===>"  As his only contribution to the speechmaking, Mr.
Unknown<===>Cecil Barr-Smith greeted this sentiment with a hearty "Hear, hear.
Unknown<===>" He fell into step with Antonia as we left the pavilion.
Unknown<===>Then he went back as if to look for something; and I saw Antonia summon Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins to her side so that she might congratulate him on the success of this "carouse.
Unknown<===>"  Everything seemed going well.
Unknown<===>There was, however, in that gathering, as in the day, material for a storm, and I, of all those in attendance, ought to have seen it, had my memory been as unerring as I thought it.
Unknown<===>CHAPTER XI.
Unknown<===>The Empress and Sir John Meet Again.
Unknown<===>The company emerged from the tent into the enchanted outdoors of the star-dotted valley.
Unknown<===>The moon rode high, and flooded the glades with silvery effulgency.
Unknown<===>The heat of the day had bred a summer storm-cloud, which, all quivery with lightning, seemed sweeping around from the northwest to the north, giving us the delicious experience of enjoying calm, in view of storm.
Unknown<===>The music of the orchestra soon told that the pavilion had been cleared for dancing.
Unknown<===>I heard Giddings urging upon Miss Addison that it would be much better for them to walk in the moonlight than to encourage by their presence such a worldly amusement, and one in which he had never been able to do anything better than fail, anyhow.
Unknown<===>Sighing her pain at the frivolity of the world, she took his arm and strolled away.
Unknown<===>I noticed that she clung closely to him, frightened, I suppose, at the mysterious rustlings in the trees, or something.
Unknown<===>They made up the dances in such a way as to leave me out.
Unknown<===>I rather wanted to dance with Antonia; but Mr.
Unknown<===>Cecil was just leaving her in disappointment, in the possession of Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins, when I went for her.
Unknown<===>I decided that a cigar and solitude were rather to be chosen than anything else which presented itself, and accordingly I took possession of one of the hammocks, in which I lay and smoked, and watched the towering thunder-head, as it stood like a mighty and marvelous mountain in the northern sky, its rounded and convoluted summits serenely white in the moonlight, its mysterious caves palpitant with incessant lightning.
Unknown<===>The soothing of the cigar; the new-made lake reflecting the gleam of hundreds of lanterns; the illuminated pavilion, its whirling company of dancers seen under the uprolled walls; the night, with its strange contrast of a calm southern sky on the one hand pouring down its flood of moonlight, and in the north the great mother-of-pearl dome with its core of vibrant fire; the dance-music throbbing through the lindens; and all this growing out of the unwonted and curious life of the past few months, bore to me again that feeling of being yoked with some thaumaturge of wondrous power for the working of enchantments.
Unknown<===>Again I seemed in a partnership with Aladdin; and fairy pavilions, sylvan paradises, bevies of dancing girls, and princes bearing gifts of gold and jewels, had all obeyed our conjuration.
Unknown<===>I could have walked down to the naphtha pleasure-boat and bidden the engineer put me down at Khorassan, or some dreamful port of far Cathay, with no sense of incongruity.
Unknown<===>Two figures came from the tent and walked toward me.
Unknown<===>As I looked at them, myself in darkness, they in the light, I had again that feeling of having seen them in some similar way before.
Unknown<===>That same old sensation, thought I, that the analytic novelist made trite ages ago.
Unknown<===>Then I saw that it was Mr.
Unknown<===>Cornish and Miss Trescott.
Unknown<===>I could hear them talking; but lay still, because I was loth to have my reveries disturbed.
Unknown<===>And besides, to speak would seem an unwarranted assumption of confidential relations on their part.
Unknown<===>They stopped near me.
Unknown<===>"Your memory is not so good as mine," said he.
Unknown<===>"I knew you at once.
Unknown<===>Knew you.
Unknown<===>Why--"  "I'm not very good at keeping names and faces in mind," she replied, "unless they belong to people I have known very well.
Unknown<===>"  "Indeed.
Unknown<===>" his voice dropped to the 'cello-like undertone now; "isn't that a little unkind.
Unknown<===>I fancied that _we_ knew each other very well.
Unknown<===>My conceit is not to be pandered to, I perceive.
Unknown<===>"  "Ye-e-s--does it seem that way.
Unknown<===>" said she, ignoring the last remark.
Unknown<===>"Well, you know it was only for a few days, and you kept calling yourself by some ridiculous alias, and scarcely used your surname at all, and I believe they called you Johnny--and you can't think what a disguise such a beard is.
Unknown<===>But I remember you now perfectly.
Unknown<===>It quite brings back those short months, when I was so young--and was finding things out.
Unknown<===>I can see the vine-covered porch, and Madame Lamoreaux's boarding-house on the South Side--"  "And the old art gallery.
Unknown<===>"  "Why, there was one, wasn't there.
Unknown<===>" said she, "somewhere along the lake front, wasn't it.
Unknown<===>Such a pleasant meeting, and so odd.
Unknown<===>"  I sat up in the hammock, and stared at them as they went on their promenade.
Unknown<===>The old art gallery, the vine-covered porch, the young man with the smooth-shaven dark face and the thrilling, vibrant voice, and the young, young girl with the ruddy hair, and the little, round form.
Unknown<===>She seemed taller now, and there was more of maturity in the figure; but it was the same lissome waist and petite gracefulness which had so fully explained to me the avid eyes of her lover on that day when I had fled from the report of the Committee on Permanent Organization.
Unknown<===>It was the Empress Josephine, I had known that--and her Sir John.
Unknown<===>Then I thought of her flying from him into the street, and the little bowed head on the street-car; and the old pity for her, the old bitterness toward him, returned upon me.
Unknown<===>I wondered how he could speak to her in this nonchalant way; what they were saying to each other; whether they would ever refer to that night at Auriccio's; what Alice would think of him if she ever found it out; whether he was a villain, or only erred passionately; what was actually said in that palm alcove that night so long ago; whether this man, with the eyes and voice so fascinating to women, would renew his suit in this new life of ours; what Jim would think about it; and, more than all, how Josie herself would regard him.
Unknown<===>"She ought never to have spoken to him again.
Unknown<===>" I hear some one say.
Unknown<===>Ah, Madam, very true.
Unknown<===>But do you remember any authentic case of a woman who failed to forgive the man whose error or offense had for its excuse the irresistible attraction of her own charms.
Unknown<===>They were coming back now, still talking.
Unknown<===>"You dropped out of sight, like a partridge into a thicket," said he.
Unknown<===>"Some of them said you had gone back to--to--"  "To the farm," she prompted.
Unknown<===>"Well, yes," he conceded; "and others said you had left Chicago for New York; and some, even Paris.
Unknown<===>"  "I fail to see the warrant," said Josie, as they approached the limit of earshot, "for any of the people at Madame Lamoreux's giving themselves the trouble to investigate.
Unknown<===>"  "So far as that is concerned," said he, "I should think that I--" and his voice quite lost intelligibility.
Unknown<===>My cigar had gone out, and the cessation of the music ought to have apprised me of the breaking up of the dance, and still I lay looking at the sky and filled with my thoughts.
Unknown<===>"Here he is," said Alice, "asleep in the hammock.
Unknown<===>For shame, Albert.
Unknown<===>This would not have occurred, once.
Unknown<===>"  "I am free to admit that," said I, "but why am I now disturbed.
Unknown<===>"  "We're going on a cruise in the gondola," said Antonia, "and Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins says you are lieutenant, and we can't sail without you.
Unknown<===>Come, it's perfectly beautiful out there.
Unknown<===>"  "We're going to the head of navigation and back," said Jim, "and then our revels will be ended.
Unknown<===>--Hang it.
Unknown<===>" to me, "they left the skull and crossbones off all the flags.
Unknown<===>"  Mr.
Unknown<===>Barr-Smith at once engaged the engineer in conversation, and seemed worming from him all his knowledge of the construction of the boat.
Unknown<===>The rest of us lounged on cushions and seats.
Unknown<===>We threaded our way up the new pond, winding between clumps of trees, now in broad moonlight, now in deepest shade.
Unknown<===>The shower had swept over to the northeast, just one dark flounce of its skirt reaching to the zenith.
Unknown<===>A cool breeze suddenly sprang up from the west, stirred by the suction of the receding storm, and a roar came from the trees on the hilltops.
Unknown<===>"Better run for port," said Jim; "I'd hate to have Mr.
Unknown<===>Barr-Smith suffer shipwreck where the charts don't show any water.
Unknown<===>"  As we ran down the open way, the remark seemed less and less of a joke.
Unknown<===>The gale poured over the hills, and struck the boat like the buffet of a great hand.
Unknown<===>She heeled over alarmingly, bumped upon a submerged stump, righted, heeled again, this time shipping a little sea, and then the sharp end of a hidden oak-limb thrust up through the bottom, and ripped its way out again, leaving us afloat in the deepest part of the lake, with a spouting fountain in the middle of the vessel, and the chopping waves breaking over the gunwale.
Unknown<===>All at once, I noticed Cecil Barr-Smith, with his coat off, standing near Antonia, who sat as cool as if she had been out on some quiet road driving her pacers.
Unknown<===>The boat sank lower in the water, and I had no doubt that she was sinking.
Unknown<===>Antonia rose, and stretched her hands towards Jim.
Unknown<===>I do not see how he could avoid seeing this; but he did, and, as if abandoning her to her fate, he leaped to Josie's side.
Unknown<===>Cornish had seized _her_ by the arm, and seemed about to devote himself to her safety, when Jim, without a word, lifted her in his arms, and leaped lightly upon the forward deck, the highest and driest place on the sinking craft.
Unknown<===>Then, as everything pointed to a speedy baptism in the lake for all of us, we saw that the very speed of the wind had saved us, and felt the gondola bump broadside upon the dam.
Unknown<===>Jim sprang to the abutment with Josie, and Cecil Barr-Smith half carried and half led Antonia to the shore.
Unknown<===>Alice and I sat calmly on the windward rail; and Barr-Smith, laughing with delight, helped us across, one at a time, to the masonry.
Unknown<===>"I'm glad it turned out no worse," said Jim.
Unknown<===>"I hope you will all excuse me if I leave you now.
Unknown<===>I must see Miss Trescott to a safe and dry place.
Unknown<===>Here's the carriage, Josie.
Unknown<===>"  "Are you quite uninjured.
Unknown<===>" said Cecil to Antonia, as Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins and Josie drove away.
Unknown<===>"Oh, quite so.
Unknown<===>" said Antonia, unwittingly adopting Barr-Smith's phrase.
Unknown<===>"But for a moment I was awfully frightened.
Unknown<===>"  "It looked a little damp, at one time, for farce-comedy," said Cornish.
Unknown<===>"I wonder how deep it was out there.
Unknown<===>"  "Miss Trescott was quite drenched," said Mr.
Unknown<===>Barr-Smith, as we got into the carriages.
Unknown<===>"Too bad, by Jove.
Unknown<===>"  "You may write home," said Antonia, "an account of being shipwrecked in the top of a tree.
Unknown<===>"  "Good, good.
Unknown<===>" said Cecil, and we all joined in the laugh, until we were suddenly sobered by the fact that Antonia had bowed her head on Alice's lap, and was sobbing as if her heart was broken.
Unknown<===>CHAPTER XII.
Unknown<===>In which the Burdens of wealth begin to fall upon Us.
Unknown<===>If the town be considered as a quiescent body pursuing its unluminous way in space, Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins may stand for the impinging planet which shocked it into vibrant life.
Unknown<===>I suggested this nebular-hypothesis simile to Mr.
Unknown<===>Giddings, one day, as the germ of an editorial.
Unknown<===>"It's rather seductive," said he, "but it won't do.
Unknown<===>Carry your interplanetary collision business to its logical end, and what do you come to.
Unknown<===>Gaseousness.
Unknown<===>And that's just what the Angus Falls _Times_, the Fairchild Star, and the other loathsome sheets printed in prairie-dog towns around here accuse us of, now.
Unknown<===>No; much obliged; but as a field for comparisons the tried old solar system is good enough for the _Herald_.
Unknown<===>"  I couldn't help thinking, however, that the thing had some illustrative merit.
Unknown<===>There was Jim's first impact, felt locally, and jarring things loose.
Unknown<===>Then came the atomic vivification, the heat and motion, which appeared in the developments which we have seen taking form.
Unknown<===>After the visit of the Barr-Smiths, and the immigration of Cornish, the new star Lattimore began to blaze in the commercial firmament, the focus of innumerable monetary telescopes, pointed from the observatories of counting-rooms, banks, and offices, far and wide.
Unknown<===>There was a shifting of the investment and speculative equilibrium, and things began coming to us spontaneously.
Unknown<===>The Angus Falls railway extension was won only by strenuous endeavor.
Unknown<===>Captain Tolliver's interviews with General Lattimore, in which he was so ruthlessly "turned down," he always regarded as a sort of creative agony, marking the origin of the roundhouse and machine-shops, and our connection with the great Halliday railway system of which it made us a part.
Unknown<===>The street-car project went more easily; and, during the autumn, the geological and manufacturing experts sent out to report on the cement-works enterprise, pronounced favorably, and gangs of men, during the winter, were to be seen at work on the foundations of the great buildings by the scarped chalk-hill.
Unknown<===>The tension of my mind just after the Lynhurst Park affair was such as to attune it to no impulses but the financial vibrations which pulsated through our atmosphere.
Unknown<===>True, I sometimes felt the wonder return upon me at the finding of the lovers of the art-gallery together once more, in Josie and Cornish; and at other times Antonia's agitation after our escape from shipwreck recurred to me in contrast with her smiling self-possession while the boat was drifting and filling; but mostly I thought of nothing, dreamed of nothing, but trust companies, additions, bonds and mortgages.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Barr-Smith returned to London soon, giving a parting luncheon in his rooms, where wine flowed freely, and toasts of many colors were pushed into the atmosphere.
Unknown<===>There was one to the President and the Queen, proposed by the host and drunk in bumpers, and others to Mr.
Unknown<===>Barr-Smith, his brother, and the members of the "Syndicate.
Unknown<===>" The enthusiasm grew steadily in intensity as the affair progressed.
Unknown<===>Finally Mr.
Unknown<===>Cecil solemnly proposed "The American Woman.
Unknown<===>" In offering this toast, he said, he was taking long odds, as it was a sport for which he hadn't had the least training; but he couldn't forego the pleasure of paying a tribute where tribute was due.
Unknown<===>The ladies of America needed no encomiums from him, and yet he was sure that he should give no offense by saying that they were of a type unknown in history.
Unknown<===>They were up to anything, you know, in the way of intellectuality, and he was sure that in a certain queenly, blonde way they were--  "Hear, hear.
Unknown<===>" said his brother, and burst into a laugh in which we all joined, while Cecil went on talking, in an uproar which drowned his words, though one could see that he was trying to explain something, and growing very hot in the process.
Unknown<===>Pearson announced that their train would soon arrive, and we all went down to see them off.
Unknown<===>Barr-Smith assured us at parting that the tram-road transaction might be considered settled.
Unknown<===>He believed, too, that his clients might come into the cement project.
Unknown<===>We were all the more hopeful of this, for the knowledge that he carried somewhere in his luggage a bond for a deed to a considerable interest in the cement lands.
Unknown<===>Things were coming on beautifully; and it seemed as if Elkins and Cornish, working together, were invincible.
Unknown<===>We still lived at the hotel, but our architect, "little Ed.
Unknown<===>Smith, who lived over on the Hayes place" when we were boys, and who was once at Garden City with Jim, was busy with plans for a mansion which we were to build in the new Lynhurst Park Addition the next spring.
Unknown<===>Mr.
Unknown<===>Elkins was preparing to erect a splendid house in the same neighborhood.
Unknown<===>"Can I afford it.
Unknown<===>" said I, in discussing estimates.
Unknown<===>"Afford it.
Unknown<===>" he replied, turning on me in astonishment.
Unknown<===>"My dear boy, don't you see we are up against a situation that calls on us to bluff to the limit, or lay down.
Unknown<===>In such a case, luxury becomes a duty, and lavishness the truest economy.
Unknown<===>Not to spend is to go broke.
Unknown<===>Lay your Poor Richard on the shelf, and put a weight on him.
Unknown<===>Stimulate the outgo, and the income'll take care of itself.
Unknown<===>A thousand spent is five figures to the good.
Unknown<===>No, while we've as many boom-irons in the fire as we're heating now, to be modest is to be lost.
Unknown<===>"  "Perhaps," said I, "you may be right, and no doubt are.
Unknown<===>We'll talk it over again some time.
Unknown<===>And your remark about irons in the fire brings up another matter which bothers me.
Unknown<===>It's something unusual when we don't open up a set of books for some new corporation, during the working day.
Unknown<===>Aren't we getting too many.
Unknown<===>"  "Do you remember Mule Jones, who lived down near Hickory Grove.
Unknown<===>" said he, after a long pause.
Unknown<===>"Well, you know, in our old neighborhood, the mule was regarded with a mixture of contempt, suspicion, and fear, the folks not understanding him very well, and being especially uninformed as to his merits.
Unknown<===>Therefore, Mule Jones, who dealt in mules, bought, sold, and broke 'em, was a man of mark, and identified in name with his trade, as most people used to be before our time.
Unknown<===>I was down there one Sunday, and asked him how he managed to break the brutes.
Unknown<===>'It's easy,' said he, 'when you know how.
Unknown<===>I never hook up less'n six of 'em at a time.
Unknown<===>Then they sort o' neutralize one another.
Unknown<===>Some on 'em'll be r'arin' an' pitchin', an' some tryin' to run; but they'll be enough of 'em down an' a-draggin' all the time, to keep the enthusiastic ones kind o' suppressed, and give me the castin' vote.
Unknown<===>It's the only right way to git the bulge on mules.
Unknown<===>' Whenever you get to worrying about our various companies, think of the Mule Jones system and be calm.
Unknown<===>"  "I'm a little shy of being ruled by one case, even though so exactly in point," said I.
Unknown<===>"Well, it's all right," he continued, "and about these houses.
Unknown<===>Why, we'd have to build them, even if we preferred to live in tents.
Unknown<===>Put the cost in the advertising account of Lynhurst Park Addition, if it worries you.
Unknown<===>Let me ask you, now, as a reasonable man, how can we expect the rest of the world to come out here and spring themselves for humble dwellings with stationary washtubs, conservatories, and _porte cocheres_, if we ourselves haven't any more confidence in the deal than to put up Jim Crow wickiups costing not more than ten or fifteen thousand dollars apiece.
Unknown<===>That addition has got to be the Nob Hill of Lattimore.
Unknown<===>Nothing in the 'poor but honest' line will do for Lynhurst; and we've got to set the pace.
Unknown<===>When you see my modest bachelor quarters going up, you'll cease to think of yours in the light of an extravagance.
Unknown<===>By next fall you'll be infested with money, anyhow, and that house will be the least of your troubles.
Unknown<===>"  Alice and I made up our minds that Jim was right, and went on with our plans on a scale which sometimes brought back the Aladdin idea to my mind, accustomed as I was to rural simplicity.
Unknown<===>But Alice, notwithstanding that she was the daughter of a country physician of not very lucrative practice, rose to the occasion, and spent money with a spontaneous largeness of execution which revealed a genius hitherto unsuspected by either of us.
Unknown<===>Jim was thoroughly delighted with it.
Unknown<===>"The Republic," he argued, "cannot be in any real danger when the modest middle classes produce characters of such strength in meeting great emergencies.
Unknown<===>"  Jim was at his best this summer.
Unknown<===>He revelled in the work of filling the morning paper with scare-heads detailing our operations.
Unknown<===>He enjoyed being It, he said.
Unknown<===>Cornish, after the first few days, during which, in spite of inside information as to his history, I felt that he would make good the predictions of the _Herald_, ceased to be, in my mind, anything more than I was--a trusted aide of Jim, the general.
Unknown<===>Both men went rather frequently out to the Trescott farm--Jim with the bluff freedom of a brother, Cornish with his rather ceremonious deference.
Unknown<===>I distrusted the dark Sir John where women were concerned, noting how they seemed charmed by him; but I could not see that he had made any headway in regaining Josie's regard, though I had a lurking feeling that he meant to do so.
Unknown<===>I saw at times in his eyes the old look which I remembered so well.
Unknown<===>Josie, more than ever this season, was earning her father's commendation as his "right-hand man.
Unknown<===>" She insisted on driving the four horses which drew the binder in the harvest.
Unknown<===>In the haying she operated the horse-rake, and helped man the hay-fork in filling the barns.
Unknown<===>She grew as tanned as if she had spent the time at the seashore or on the links; and with every month she added to her charm.
Unknown<===>The scarlet of her lips, the ruddy luxuriance of her hair, the arrowy straightness of her carriage, the pulsing health which beamed from her eye, and dyed cheek and neck, made their appeal to the women, even.
Unknown<===>"How sweet she is.
Unknown<===>" said Alice, as she came to greet us one day when we drove to the farm, and waited for her to come to us.
Unknown<===>"How sweet she is, Albert.
Unknown<===>"  Her father came up, and explained to us that he didn't ask any of his women folks to do any work except what there was in the house.
Unknown<===>He was able to hire the outdoors work done, but Josie he couldn't keep out of the fields.
Unknown<===>"Why, pa," said she, "don't you see you would spoil my chances of marrying a fairy prince.
Unknown<===>They absolutely never come into the house; and my straw hat is the only really becoming thing I've got to wear.
Unknown<===>"  "Don't give a dum if yeh never marry," said Bill.
Unknown<===>"Hain't seen the man yit that was good enough fer yeh, from my standpoint.
Unknown<===>"  Bill's reputation was pretty well known to me by this time.
Unknown<===>He had been for years a successful breeder and shipper of live-stock, in which vocation he had become well-to-do.
Unknown<===>On his farm he was forceful and efficient, treading his fields like an admiral his quarter-deck.
Unknown<===>About town he was given to talking horses and cattle with the groups which frequented the stables and blacksmith-shops, and sometimes grew a little noisy and boisterous with them.
Unknown<===>Whenever her father went with a shipment of cattle to Chicago or other market, Josie went too, taking a regular passenger train in time to be waiting when Bill's stock train arrived; and after the beeves were disposed of, Bill became her escort to opera and art-gallery; on such a visit I had seen her at the Stock Yards.
Unknown<===>She was fond of her father; but this alone did not explain her constant attendance upon him.
Unknown<===>I soon came to understand that his prompt return from the city, in good condition, was apt to be dependent upon her influence.
Unknown<===>It was one of those cases of weakness, associated with strength, the real mystery of which does not often occur to us because they are so common.
Unknown<===>He came into our office one day with a tremor in his hand and a hunted look in his eye.
Unknown<===>He took a chair at my invitation, but rose at once, went to the door, and looked up and down the street, as if for pursuers.
Unknown<===>I saw Captain Tolliver across the street, and Bill's air of excitement was explained.
Unknown<===>I was relieved, for at first I had thought him intoxicated.
Unknown<===>"What's the matter, Bill.
Unknown<===>" said I, after he had looked at me earnestly, almost pantingly, for a few moments.
Unknown<===>"You look nervous.
Unknown<===>"  "They're after me," he answered in repressed tones, "to sell; and I'll be blasted if I know what to do.
Unknown<===>Wha' d'ye' 'spose they're offerin' me for my land.
Unknown<===>"  "The fact is, Bill," said I, "that I know all about it.
Unknown<===>I'm interested in the deal, somewhat.
Unknown<===>"  "Then you know they've bid right around a thousand dollars an acre.
Unknown<===>"  "Yes," said I, "or at least that they intended to offer that.
Unknown<===>"  "An' you're one o' the company," he queried, "that's doin' it.
Unknown<===>"  "Yes," I admitted.
